<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_7cb48234-bc46-42d4-be21-03b59cf2ce29'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }
  //]]>
</script>

<span id="freeTextContainer18080374860688323580">Riley has crossed the bridge into the afterlife—a place called Here, where time is always Now. She has picked up life where she left off when she was alive, living with her parents and dog in a nice house in a nice neighborhood.   <span id="freeText18080374860688323580" style="display:none">Riley has crossed the bridge into the afterlife—a place called Here, where time is always Now. She has picked up life where she left off when she was alive, living with her parents and dog in a nice house in a nice neighborhood. When she's summoned before The Council, she learns that the afterlife isn't just an eternity of leisure. She's been assigned a job, Soul Catcher, and a teacher, Bodhi, a possibly cute, seemingly nerdy boy who's definitely hiding something. They return to earth together for Riley's first assignment, a Radiant Boy who's been haunting a castle in England for centuries. Many Soul Catchers have tried to get him to cross the bridge and failed. But all of that was before he met Riley . . .<br /><br /><i>Radiance </i>is the first book in the Riley Bloom series from bestselling author Alyson Noël.</span>

<div id="review_510208749" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/510208749" />
    <a title="Liz" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14811808-liz"><img alt="Liz" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585394064p2/14811808.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/510208749?book_show_action=true">Jan 18, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Liz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Liz" href="/user/show/14811808-liz">Liz</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14811808-liz?shelf=i-prefer-rum">i-prefer-rum</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14811808-liz?shelf=headdesk-not-sorry">headdesk-not-sorry</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer510208749" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18279141070916698308">Damn, I don't know what is worse: This series or The Immortals. <br/><br/><br/>Just a brief summary: <br/>Riley is dead, but she cannot accept it. She wants to go back and live a proper teenager life. She does not like the Here she is living in now. <br/>Neither does she like the fact that she has a job to do. A pretty "dangerous" and "hard" one. <br/><br/>Sounds okay, right? I thought: Well, the other series was nothing for me but maybe this one will be better. <br/>It is not. <br/><br/>Riley is a spoiled, annoying girl who sometimes talks lik</span>
  <span id="freeText18279141070916698308" style="display:none">Damn, I don't know what is worse: This series or The Immortals. <br><br><br>Just a brief summary: <br>Riley is dead, but she cannot accept it. She wants to go back and live a proper teenager life. She does not like the Here she is living in now. <br>Neither does she like the fact that she has a job to do. A pretty "dangerous" and "hard" one. <br><br>Sounds okay, right? I thought: Well, the other series was nothing for me but maybe this one will be better. <br>It is not. <br><br>Riley is a spoiled, annoying girl who sometimes talks like she is a 10 and sometimes like a grown-up woman. This is sort of confusing and unrealistic. It seems like sometimes the author is talking and sometimes the character.<br>Even more annoying is the fact, that she cannot accept her dead. I mean, honestly, does this girl think you can magically return and live like nothing happened? When you die, there is no come-back. Sorry to disappoint. <br>Bodhi... Awkward. This is the perfect word to describe this guy. <br>Oh, and then, there is the Radiant boy. Or rather three of them. Three <br>10-years-old boys who want fame...<b>Are you kidding me?!</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/381074.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Oh, and Riley, of course, is the only one who is not afraid of three little kids. She manages to persuade them to go and stop hunting the place. Wow, Riley is such a hero! <br>I hoped that maybe the Last Judgment would be normal. It wasn't. <br>The Author managed to make all of them funny, unrealistic and ridiculous. Congratulations!<br><br>Pointless plot, no development, pointless characters, unrealistic dialogues. This is what I think about this book.<br>Nothing but a waste of time.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/480424.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4176166-cindy?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4176166-cindy?shelf=sci-fi-fantasy">sci-fi-fantasy</a>,

<span id="freeTextContainer9555922914186021936"><b>This review may also be found on <a><i>A Thousand Little Pages</i></a>.</b><br/><br/>Having read a bit of Alyson Noel’s paranormal series <i>The Immortals</i> before, I started <i>Radiance</i> with expectations. The beautiful pastel blue cover and the rolling field of blue flowers were undoubtedly attracting factors. However, <i>Radiance</i> proved to be less gorgeous than its cover -- far less. After the first few pages, it became just another one of those mediocre what-life-is-like-after-you-die YA stories. For me, this type of plot is eithe</span>
  <span id="freeText9555922914186021936" style="display:none"><b>This review may also be found on <a><i>A Thousand Little Pages</i></a>.</b><br><br>Having read a bit of Alyson Noel’s paranormal series <i>The Immortals</i> before, I started <i>Radiance</i> with expectations. The beautiful pastel blue cover and the rolling field of blue flowers were undoubtedly attracting factors. However, <i>Radiance</i> proved to be less gorgeous than its cover -- far less. After the first few pages, it became just another one of those mediocre what-life-is-like-after-you-die YA stories. For me, this type of plot is either a hit or a miss. <i>Radiance</i> was a miss.<br><br>A round of applause goes to the protagonist, Riley Bloom, for securing a spot on my characters-I-would-like-to-maim list. Seriously, has there <i>ever</i> been a more annoying 12-year-old girl in the history of YA lit? Since the story is in first person, the reader gets <i>treated</i> to 24/7 updates on Riley’s feelings as she complains and worries and complains and worries some more. The puppy love set up in here was also totally unnecessary. If the romance doesn’t aid the plot or spice it up for the reader, why bother putting it there? The entire book read like a novella, with barely any build-up of tension and a climax that was not climatic at all.<br><br>There was one line in <i>Radiance</i> that really got me, and not exactly in a positive way, either. So Riley, who just so happens to be <i>complaining</i> about the lack of fashion sense of a particular guy, remarks: “Just close your eyes and ask -- What would Joe Jonas wear?<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380340331i/696761.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>OK, mentioning the Jonas Brothers (who I just so happen to dislike immensely) is called failure. Failure failure failure… Alyson Noel also mentions good ol’ Robert Pattinson, to which I responded with headKindle -- banging my head frustratingly on my Kindle to relieve stress.<br><br>I always prefer to end reviews on a positive note, so here it is: <i>Radiance</i> used the word “discombobulated” twice. I think this is the first time I’ve seen that delightful word in a published book!<br><br>Will I be picking up the sequel <i>Shimmer</i>? No. But I do feel that this book was geared toward younger teens. Maybe kids below the age of 13 would gobble this stuff up like pie...<br><br>Book Source: Borrowed</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12763230932137767979">REVIEW<br/>I felt like I hit the jackpot when I read Radiance. It has a feisty girl as the main character, a lovably dorky boy, and a loyal dog. Add a plot with unexpected twists and a completely stunning ending and you’ve got one sweet novel. <br/>One of my favorite parts about this book was the idea of Here and Now.   <span id="freeText12763230932137767979" style="display:none">REVIEW<br />I felt like I hit the jackpot when I read Radiance. It has a feisty girl as the main character, a lovably dorky boy, and a loyal dog. Add a plot with unexpected twists and a completely stunning ending and you’ve got one sweet novel. <br />One of my favorite parts about this book was the idea of Here and Now. An enchanted place where everything you wish for comes true. If you wish to live at the ocean, then you live at the ocean. Here and Now is only limited by your imagination.<br />I also loved the characters because they were so real to this tween girl. Riley was a girl with attitude and Bodhi was such a geek that it was cute. I’m not just talking about the people characters though. Buttercup’s devotion to Riley made me wish she were my dog.<br />So, I mentioned the ending was stunning, but that doesn’t really do it justice. It was one of the most unique endings I have ever read. SWEETNESS!<br />Radiance is Alyson Noel’s first middle grade book. I am looking forward to the follow-up book, Shimmer. I am also going to check out her YA series, The Immortals. <br />RATING<br />5 Plot<br />5 Characters<br />4 Attention Grabbing<br />4 Girlie Meter<br />5 Ending<br /><br />23 TOTAL<br /><br />5 STARS</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11033070460060623714">It's been a long time since I read the Evermore series, so it took me a while to realize that the main girl in this book is Ever's younger sister.   <span id="freeText11033070460060623714" style="display:none">It's been a long time since I read the Evermore series, so it took me a while to realize that the main girl in this book is Ever's younger sister. I think it's cool that she gets her own middle grade series and we see what she is up to in the afterlife. The way the author describes the afterlife is interesting, you help others and become a better person and sort of level up. Each level comes with it's own perks and you can still watch your loved ones that are alive if you want. <br />Riley can be a bit annoying, but she's twelve so I'll forgive her. She's the little sister who wants to be you and know all about your life. I liked seeing her grow a bit and help others. I think her friendship with Bodhi may develop into more down the road, hopefully when she's older. This was a short, easy read with a cute story. </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_137128446" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/137128446" />
    <a title="Karissa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4057501-karissa"><img alt="Karissa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557318686p2/4057501.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/137128446?book_show_action=true">Dec 29, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Karissa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Karissa" href="/user/show/4057501-karissa">Karissa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer137128446" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6291611005758897341">I have been curious about Alyson Noel's The Immortals series, but because of mediocre reviews haven't wanted to commit to such a long series. When I saw that Noel had released a short novel that was a spin-off of the series I thought it would be a great way to get a feel for her writing and see if I wanted to read more by her. This book was okay, but the character's were a bit flat and immature for me.<br/><br/>Riley is dead and is living in the Hear and Now. Her parents are there and her house is there. </span>
  <span id="freeText6291611005758897341" style="display:none">I have been curious about Alyson Noel's The Immortals series, but because of mediocre reviews haven't wanted to commit to such a long series. When I saw that Noel had released a short novel that was a spin-off of the series I thought it would be a great way to get a feel for her writing and see if I wanted to read more by her. This book was okay, but the character's were a bit flat and immature for me.<br /><br />Riley is dead and is living in the Hear and Now. Her parents are there and her house is there. Everything is kind of the same as it was when she was alive. Then on her first day of school things go wrong, she can't find her place...her job... in the Here and Now. When she is called before the Council they decide she should be a Soul Catcher and assign super-geek Bodhi to be her guide. Now Riley has to try and travel back to the land of the living to complete her assignment.<br /><br />As far as ghost stories go, this one didn't really add anything to the genre that hadn't been done before. Riley is basically somewhere in between the land of the living and Heaven and is having trouble accepting that. I think this book is written at a lower age level than The Immortals because it is being told from Riley's perspective (she is thirteen years old).<br /><br />The writing style for this book is okay, if a bit juvenile. It is readable and engaging. My biggest problem with this book are the characters. None of them are all that likable and they are also stereotypical. Riley is shallow, obnoxious, and whiny. Right away she starts giving Bodhi a hard time because he looks geeky; then later when he has his geeky glasses off she is all like "Oh, swoon he is so hot." I mean really how shallow can you be? Bodhi as a character isn't much better, although the fact that he even tolerates Riley says he's got more going on than she does. I think Riley is supposed to come off as snarky; but in reality she is irritating and obnoxious...even she realizes this at points...but she makes no effort to change.<br /><br />Overall not a book I enjoyed much. The biggest thing this book had going for it is that the dialogue was natural sounding and readable (if obnoxious) and it was a really short book. Personally I wouldn't waste my time on this book unless you are a serious die-hard fan of the Immortals series. There wasn't much story here, not much creativity, and the characters were obnoxious. This book convinced me to give credence to the mediocre reviews I have been seeing for The Immortals; I don't think this author is for me. It does look like Noel is planning to write additional novels with Riley and Bodhi; so if you do enjoy this book you should have more of the same to look forward to in the future.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6291611005758897341" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText15105476350731466787" style="display:none">Okay, so since I never actually finished the Evermore Series.. I had no idea that this series was about her younger sister. Riley was just completely and utterly herself. A preteen who longed to become a teenager and died before she could ever see the age of 13. I still annoy her today. <br /><br />Other than that, I adored her friendship with Bodhi. I'm not sure what's going to happen with them down the road but for right now, they were cute and I liked them. </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9788580570533" href="/book/show/13254579-radiante">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83313012-haytham-reid?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83313012-haytham-reid?shelf=read-it-in-portuguese">read-it-in-portuguese</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83313012-haytham-reid?shelf=sigh">sigh</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3305412556" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6716907944870655625">I picked up this book thinking it would be like one of those Wattpad stories about angels and the afterlife that, back in the day, were the absolute <i>rage</i>. I always loved those types of stories: the adventure, the mysticism and even the romance. Despite what you may be thinking, there were works published on Wattpad with actual talent and effort put into them.<br/><br/>Unfortunately for <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17332218.Words_of_Radiance__The_Stormlight_Archive___2_' title='Words of Radiance (The Stormlight Archive, #2) by Brandon Sanderson' rel='nofollow noopener'> Radiance</a>, this ain't it. It's as mediocre - if not worse - as your run-of-the-mill fanfiction or your typical crappy YA.</span>
  <span id="freeText6716907944870655625" style="display:none">I picked up this book thinking it would be like one of those Wattpad stories about angels and the afterlife that, back in the day, were the absolute <i>rage</i>. I always loved those types of stories: the adventure, the mysticism and even the romance. Despite what you may be thinking, there were works published on Wattpad with actual talent and effort put into them.<br><br>Unfortunately for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17332218.Words_of_Radiance__The_Stormlight_Archive___2_" title="Words of Radiance (The Stormlight Archive, #2) by Brandon Sanderson" rel="nofollow noopener"> Radiance</a>, this ain't it. It's as mediocre - if not worse - as your run-of-the-mill fanfiction or your typical crappy YA. I can see this being amazing for a kid but it doesn't translate well for an adult or even a teenager.<br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17332218.Words_of_Radiance__The_Stormlight_Archive___2_" title="Words of Radiance (The Stormlight Archive, #2) by Brandon Sanderson" rel="nofollow noopener"> Radiance</a> tells the story of twelve-year-old Riley, Ever's sister (Ever from <i>The Immortal</i> series. Apparently, this is a spin-off), who died in a car crash alongside her parents and her dog Buttercup. Sadly (<b>*insert sarcastic grin here*</b>), the Afterlife, known in this book as Here and Now, isn't just eternal leisure. Riley has to work as a Soul Catcher which basically consists of... <i>
  <b>you guessed it correctly!</b>
</i>, catching stubborn souls. Oh, and she has a teacher who is only two years older than her... who looks geeky but <b>
  <i>guess what!</i>
</b>, he HOT! <br><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1588158825ra/29375628.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>The one word that I'd use to describe this book is <i>inconsistent</i>. Everything, from the characters to the actual plot, was just erratic. <br>Riley sounded like a bratty, hyperactive sixteen-year-old who has a problem with controlling the words that come out of her mouth. I guess the author was trying to make her snarky and witty but she usually just came off as very sardonic and nasty. There were some good funny lines but for the most part, she was just <i>mean</i>. Riley is like that kid in middle school who straight-up bullies you when trying to roast you. <br>She also acted like a child. See the inconsistency? Sounded like an older teen, acted like a spoiled child, is, in fact, a tween. <br><br>And her parents?? That was the icing on the cake. Yeah, I get it, you're in the Here and Now and you're, ironically, enjoying "life" for the first time. But you left a sixteen-year-old kid on Earth? And you don't care?? Because you'd rather paint and listen to <i>jazz</i> instead of worrying??? And now your other kid, who's YOUNGER, is apparently embarking on a dangerous job???? And you're just "bye, bye, sweetie"????? Am I the only one that has a problem with this??????<br><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1588159065ra/29375641.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>And also: a dangerous job but Riley's dead? How dangerous can it be? There's no explanation as to why, the same way there are no real consequences or danger. Why should we worry then? We know Riley and her team are going to make it out without a scratch!<br><br>Even the pace was inconsistent!!! <i>
  <b>Good lord!</b>
</i> It was super fun to read and in the next page it was as exciting as watching paint dry. <br>The Portuguese translation is around 144 pages. I don't know about you, but considering this is an extremely short book, it should have been easy to keep a steady pace throughout the entire novel. You can still be slow-paced without being tedious and a fast-paced novel doesn't necessarily mean it's enjoyable to read. This book just couldn't decide on which one to be.<br><br>I'm also not willing to forget the Jonas Brothers and Robert Pattinson references. I'll accept the last one: I mean, it's Robert Pattinson, people, he is a fantastic actor and human being! The Jonas Brothers??? <br><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1559509789ra/27608705.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>Not that I dislike them but they're not exactly what I'd call <i>fashion icons</i>.<br><br><br>Everything about the Here and Now just felt dumb. Characters who are supposed to inspire fear and respect feel ridiculous. One of the angels was described as <i>hot</i>, like a movie star.<br><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1441405451ra/16103799.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>Not only does that make everything absolutely absurd, it's also another point on my list against Riley. She's an insufferable, judgmental prick. I thought I was an absolute pain in the ass when I was twelve but this girl takes the crown home. She judges and mocks people by their looks - including her "teacher", doesn't stop whining and is just downright mean to everybody. She respects nobody and thinks she's better than everyone around her. In a span of around 100 pages, she complained about her flat chest <i>twice</i>. ಠ_ಠ<br><br>But the ultimate sin of this book? There's a character named Bodhi. <br><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1492508483ra/22523033.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>That's it. I don't know any other thing more horrendous than that. <br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>-----------------<br><br>For a book this short, it was a tad bit too excruciating to read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6716907944870655625" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText1004527045895913832" style="display:none">This is a cute sister series, literally! Riley Bloom is Ever's sister from the 'Immortals' series by Alyson Noel. Riley has crossed the bridge into the afterlife—a place called Here, where time is always Now. She died in an auto accident and is accompanied by the family's dog, Buttercup. She helps him to the Bridge, no problem, and she even has time to help with Bohdi's assignment, the boy's stricken mother ghost. A sweet little novel to start off the cute little series, especially if you're a fan of the Immortals series. I liked it.</span>

      <span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_review_1200397807'><a id="like_count_review_1200397807" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/1200397807?resource_type=Review"><span class="likesCount">4 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it gr-button gr-button--small" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F7886302-radiance">Like</a></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_138938327" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/138938327" />
    <a title="Annabell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2133680-annabell"><img alt="Annabell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508259146p2/2133680.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/138938327?book_show_action=true">Jan 06, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Annabell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Annabell" href="/user/show/2133680-annabell">Annabell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer138938327" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12291444357393186722">Synopsis:<br/><br/>“Most people think that death is the end.<br/>The end of life–of good times–<br/>the end of, well, pretty much everything.<br/>But those people are wrong.<br/>Dead wrong.<br/>And I should know.<br/>I died almost a year ago.’<br/><br/>Welcome to the Here & Now.<br/><br/>Riley Bloom left her sister, Ever, in the world of the living and crossed the bridge into the afterlife- a place called Here, where time is always Now. Riley and her dog, Buttercup, have been reunited with her parents and are just settling into a nice, relaxing death whe</span>
  <span id="freeText12291444357393186722" style="display:none">Synopsis:<br /><br />“Most people think that death is the end.<br />The end of life–of good times–<br />the end of, well, pretty much everything.<br />But those people are wrong.<br />Dead wrong.<br />And I should know.<br />I died almost a year ago.’<br /><br />Welcome to the Here &amp; Now.<br /><br />Riley Bloom left her sister, Ever, in the world of the living and crossed the bridge into the afterlife- a place called Here, where time is always Now. Riley and her dog, Buttercup, have been reunited with her parents and are just settling into a nice, relaxing death when she’s summoned before the Council. They let her in on a secret- the afterlife isn’t just an eternity of leisure; Riley has to work. She’s been assigned a job, Soul Catcher, and a teacher, Bodhi, a curious boy she can’t quite figure out.<br /><br />Riley, Bodhi, and Buttercup return to Earth for her first assignment, a Radiant Boy who’s been haunting a castle in England for centuries. Many Soul Catchers have tried to get him to cross the bridge and failed. But all of that was before he met Riley . . .”<br /><br />Review: At first I wasn’t to open minded about reading this book. I figured the author just wrote it to capitalize on her already New York Times Best selling books, the Immortal Series. I ended up REALLY loving this book which completely surprised me because Riley annoyed me in Evermore (first book in Immortal Series).<br /><br />In Radiance, Riley is still very much a twelve year old: smart mouthed, stubborn as hell, opinionated about everything, and over dramatic. But Riley is also caring, compassionate, loving, and in search, as all young ones are, of who she is and where she really belongs.<br /><br />Radiance follows Riley as she learns to transition into her new “life” in Here. She desperately wants to fit in but at the same time she wants to remain true to herself. She changes between outfits and moods constantly, never holding back how she feels or what she thinks. That’s something I really loved about Riley! She is always true to herself, no matter what others think and even for such a young character, many her age and many much older than her, can benefit from learning from Riley. The kid has some very good nuggets of wisdom for someone so young.<br /><br />You also get to meet Bodhi or who Riley refers to as “Monsieur Dorky Guy”. Bodhi is as nerdy as one can get: dressed in a black suit with a white shirt, skinny black tie and nerd glasses, the ones with black frames and thick glass. But Riley soon learns Bodhi isn’t all nerd, he has skills and strength she wouldn’t have expected in him.<br /><br />Bodhi helps to teach Riley how to be a Soul Catcher, one who helps get the dead who have yet to cross the bridge and cross over into Here. True to form, Riley thinks getting the Radiant Boy, a spirit who has been haunting a castle for centuries causing all who stay within the castle to flee the instant they walk in, will be easy. Bodhi warns her that many before her have failed and she should take her job more serious but of course Riley doesn’t listen.<br /><br />But there’s also another reason why Bodhi has brought Riley to the castle, he has some unfinished business of his own to attend to and Riley gets stuck in the crossfire.<br /><br />Radiance is a quick and easy read. Riley and Bodhi are so much fun to read because they are always clashing. They both think they know more than they really do and are each as stubborn as bulls! The descriptions are beautifully written and you never once feel like the story is dragged out. Each character has a place and a purpose. And Riley will remind us each of our own best friend and how much we really cherish that kind of all loving, always accepting, supportive, relationship.<br /><br />This is a great book to snuggle in bed on a rainy day to read (or even a sunny one).<br /><br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://openbooksociety.com/article/book-reviews-radiance-alyson-noel/">http://openbooksociety.com/article/bo...</a><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12291444357393186722" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_186724112" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/186724112" />
    <a title="Kayleigh" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5008249-kayleigh"><img alt="Kayleigh" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1578246142p2/5008249.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/186724112?book_show_action=true">Jul 20, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kayleigh" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kayleigh" href="/user/show/5008249-kayleigh">Kayleigh</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780330526913" href="/book/show/8707650-radiance">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer186724112" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15107010240004386417">I will honestly say that I was quite disappointed with this book.<br/>I had first read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3975774.Evermore__The_Immortals___1_' title='Evermore (The Immortals, #1) by Alyson Noel' rel='nofollow noopener'>Evermore</a>, which is the first book in Alyson Noel's more popular series The Immortals, Evermore happens to be the book where Riley the main character of Radiance, appears as Ever's younger sister, who is a ghost.<br/>She was my favorite character in Evermore, which was the main thing which attracted me to reading this book. She seemed like a pretty awesome and funny character. But this did not follow through in Radiance,</span>
  <span id="freeText15107010240004386417" style="display:none">I will honestly say that I was quite disappointed with this book.<br />I had first read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3975774.Evermore__The_Immortals___1_" title="Evermore (The Immortals, #1) by Alyson Noel" rel="nofollow noopener">Evermore</a>, which is the first book in Alyson Noel's more popular series The Immortals, Evermore happens to be the book where Riley the main character of Radiance, appears as Ever's younger sister, who is a ghost.<br />She was my favorite character in Evermore, which was the main thing which attracted me to reading this book. She seemed like a pretty awesome and funny character. But this did not follow through in Radiance, she is quite annoying and I kind of just wanted to hit her, but I guess you can say she does well at portraying 12 year old girls.<br />Riley also quickly goes to judge her guide, Bodhi, as a dork, just from how he looks, but there is no evidence in the way he acts to support this, and well also supports my reason to hating Riley.<br /><br />The writing in the book is set in first person, from Riley's perspective, the words and writing style used with in the book, was almost perfect for her, informal and chatty, but I came across some complex words which would not be used by a 12yr old.<br /><br />The book was short, and lacked any sort of decent story-line, I do personally believe it could of been improved by making the book longer. At the beginning there was the usual 50 page introduction to the book (which was more than a quarter of the book), then it went straight into the story, where as I believe a decent book slowly progresses in the central story-line and problem.<br /><br />The whole trying to convince ghosts to cross the bridge and into the afterlife/heaven, was just not believable it was too easy and silly.<br />Riley also had to leave her parents to go and fulfill the job she receives, but has no problem with that at all, when a 12yr old in fact would, the writer almost tried to forced Riley's character to be much older than she is.<br /><br />The story had nothing that seemed to pull me into it, and I was more of skim-reading the last 100pages, than I was reading it.<br /><br />The reason this book did not receive a 1 star rating, was because it was quite bad, but not horrible, it just managed to cling onto being read-able and would be a good book for younger readers.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15107010240004386417" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_118948020" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/118948020" />
    <a title="Natalie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1969199-natalie"><img alt="Natalie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1427062916p2/1969199.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/118948020?book_show_action=true">Aug 27, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natalie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natalie" href="/user/show/1969199-natalie">Natalie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer118948020" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer623706036440087945"><b><u>In a Sentence</u>:</b> Radiance is a quick and fun middle grade read with characters that grow on you.<br/><br/><b>
  <u>My Thoughts</u>
</b><br/><br/><i>A huge thanks goes out to the people at Macmillan for giving me the opportunity to read and review this book!</i><br/><br/>I have to admit: I didn't have high expectations going into Radiance. I had previously read Evermore, the first novel in Alyson Noel's companion series, and I really didn't care for it at all. However, I don't like to define an author by one book, so I wanted to give Noel another s</span>
  <span id="freeText623706036440087945" style="display:none"><b><u>In a Sentence</u>:</b> Radiance is a quick and fun middle grade read with characters that grow on you.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>My Thoughts</u>
</b><br /><br /><i>A huge thanks goes out to the people at Macmillan for giving me the opportunity to read and review this book!</i><br /><br />I have to admit: I didn't have high expectations going into Radiance. I had previously read Evermore, the first novel in Alyson Noel's companion series, and I really didn't care for it at all. However, I don't like to define an author by one book, so I wanted to give Noel another shot. In the end, I was glad I did.<br /><br />For those of you who are more interested in YA, I do want to warn you that Radiance is more of a middle grade read. The main character is twelve, and the writing and plot style are directed towards younger readers. Not that this is a bad thing, but I wanted to give you a heads up if MG books aren't your thing.<br /><br />I really only had one issue with Radiance, and that was the writing style. As you can probably tell from the "First Lines" section of my review above, the writing is very choppy and the sentences are often cut off. I felt that this made reading Radiance like driving down a suburban highway during rush hour traffic. Stop. Go. Stop. Go. Stop. Go. You get my point.<br /><br />Other than that, I thought Radiance was slightly mediocre, but overall, enjoyable. It's a series that I'll probably buy for my eleven and thirteen year-old cousins, because I think they'd really enjoy it. If you have a cousin/daughter/sister around the same age, you might want to check out Radiance, which will be available in bookstores tomorrow!<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="623706036440087945" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Allison " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Allison " href="/user/show/3194119-allison">Allison </a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer129674908" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2377994319218042457">Right after I finished <i>Shadowland</i>, I went looking for <i>Dark Flame</i> and discovered <i>Radiance</i>. Wow. It was fun. It was fun like the first two books in the <i>Immortals</i> series were fun. It was over too quick for me too. I am looking forward to the next installment coming out in the Spring 2011. <br/><br/>What I really liked was that I could really feel the voice of a 12-year-old telling the story. She says "bum" instead of "butt" or "ass", for example. She expresses discontent that she is still "flat-chested" and </span>
  <span id="freeText2377994319218042457" style="display:none">Right after I finished <i>Shadowland</i>, I went looking for <i>Dark Flame</i> and discovered <i>Radiance</i>. Wow. It was fun. It was fun like the first two books in the <i>Immortals</i> series were fun. It was over too quick for me too. I am looking forward to the next installment coming out in the Spring 2011. <br /><br />What I really liked was that I could really feel the voice of a 12-year-old telling the story. She says "bum" instead of "butt" or "ass", for example. She expresses discontent that she is still "flat-chested" and yet she loves to play fetch with her dog. She has those flashes of mature insight beyond her years and flashes of whiny little kidness. It's all rolled into one kid, very realistically and very believably.<br /><br />The second thing I really liked about this one is that I would have no hesitation about recommending it to 5th-8th graders that I would not feel comfortable recommending the <i>Immortals</i> series to - yet. Like, it'd be nice if there were a parallel set of books to the <i>Twilight</i> series that was more appropriate for the younger folks who are getting so wrapped up in the series their older siblings are drooling over.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2377994319218042457" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2334982225" />
    <a title="Sophie P-V" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/71368296-sophie-p-v"><img alt="Sophie P-V" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1506360520p2/71368296.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2334982225?book_show_action=true">Mar 21, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sophie P-V" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sophie P-V" href="/user/show/71368296-sophie-p-v">Sophie P-V</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

    <a title="Kelley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2686314-kelley"><img alt="Kelley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1251693070p2/2686314.jpg" /></a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer319643937" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer17419792290578422343">Courtesy of Amazon<br/><br/>A CK2S K2 Recommended Read!<br/><br/>I loved Riley Bloom in Alyson Noel’s The Immortals series so I was quite excited to see Riley was getting a series of her own. Now, in Radiance, we finally get to learn more about this delightful character.<br/><br/>Riley was killed in a car accident at the age of twelve, but rather than crossing over, she decided to stay for a while with her surviving sister, Ever. Finally, Riley has crossed, with her beloved dog, into a new world only known as “Here” where th</span>
  <span id="freeText17419792290578422343" style="display:none">Courtesy of Amazon<br /><br />A CK2S K2 Recommended Read!<br /><br />I loved Riley Bloom in Alyson Noel’s The Immortals series so I was quite excited to see Riley was getting a series of her own. Now, in Radiance, we finally get to learn more about this delightful character.<br /><br />Riley was killed in a car accident at the age of twelve, but rather than crossing over, she decided to stay for a while with her surviving sister, Ever. Finally, Riley has crossed, with her beloved dog, into a new world only known as “Here” where the time is always “Now.” In many ways, Here is just like being alive, with a few exceptions. Life in Here is what people make of it, but they do have responsibilities as well, and Riley is assigned a job as a Soul Catcher.<br /><br />Riley’s instructor is Bodhi, a cute, but nerdy boy who knows so much more than he’s willing to share with her. Her first assignment is the infamous “Radiant Boy” who haunts an English castle. Many Catchers have tried convincing him to cross the bridge into Here over the centuries, but all have failed miserably. However, the irrepressible Riley is on the case, and she is determined to succeed where all the others have failed. If Riley has anything to say about it, The Radiant Boy has finally met his match!<br /><br />I have read the entire Immortals series, except the most recent, and out of all the books my favorite character still is Riley. Every time she appeared early in the series in one of her crazy costumes or her sister’s clothes, I got a chuckle out of it and she stole the show every single time. So imagine my delight to have an entire Riley-centric series! The best part is, everything I loved about Riley in her sister’s books, I have in abundance in Radiance. Riley is every bit as sassy as she ever was, complete with crazy costumes and her beloved dog.<br /><br />One thing people may wonder initially is how much character growth can a dead twelve year old have throughout a book/series? The answer is… quite a bit! I especially love exactly how we learn more about who Riley was before she died and who she is now. When she views her life as she was prior to arriving in Here, as with most children, she didn’t think she had been doing much wrong. However, as her adventures continue after being paired up with Bodhi for her new job, Riley starts to realize maybe she wasn’t all that perfect before and realizes how many seemingly inconsequential behaviors have such a huge impact on others and begins to change her ways.<br /><br />Kathleen McInerney is a perfect voice actor to perform Riley. She masters the carefree and loveable persona of Riley that made me be so drawn to Riley in the Immortals series. McInerney has a way with words that we get such a wonderful idea of what Riley and company are feeling throughout Radiance, simply by listening to the narration. Hopefully, future audio versions of the Riley Bloom series will use the same voice talent.<br /><br />© Kelley A. Hartsell, January 2011. All rights reserved.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17419792290578422343" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_118205379" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/118205379" />
    <a title="Alison" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1387872-alison"><img alt="Alison" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1357755893p2/1387872.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/118205379?book_show_action=true">Aug 23, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alison" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alison" href="/user/show/1387872-alison">Alison</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer118205379" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2218150452135818961">A fun read for the 'tween crowd.<br/><br/>Riley Bloom is not a new character to anyone who has read Alyson Noel's YA series, The Immortals, which starts with the book, Evermore (link to review). Allow me to give a little background. Riley is Ever's sister. Ever is the only survivor of a car crash that killed the rest of her family, which makes Riley...well...dead. In Evermore, Riley did a bit of haunting, and didn't want to leave her sister, but she eventually crossed over - and I shed a tear when the sis</span>
  <span id="freeText2218150452135818961" style="display:none">A fun read for the 'tween crowd.<br /><br />Riley Bloom is not a new character to anyone who has read Alyson Noel's YA series, The Immortals, which starts with the book, Evermore (link to review). Allow me to give a little background. Riley is Ever's sister. Ever is the only survivor of a car crash that killed the rest of her family, which makes Riley...well...dead. In Evermore, Riley did a bit of haunting, and didn't want to leave her sister, but she eventually crossed over - and I shed a tear when the sisters parted. The Immortals series is Ever's story, but Radiance is Riley's story after she crosses over. <br /><br />Since Ever was a teenager, her story was geared toward the YA set, but Riley is only 12, so her story is aimed at a younger reader. I thought both the storyline and the language was appropriate for the younger age group. Writing to the tween crowd can be a tricky task, and I think Alyson Noel did a fantastic job at maintaining a balance of interest without being inappropriate.<br /><br />The author creates a whole new world for Riley, called the Here, in a time called the Now, which is scary because it's new to her, but doesn't necessarily frighten her. She begins her afterlife in the Here and Now with her parents and her dog, and sets off for her first day of "school." She quickly realizes that school is not what she thinks it is, and the afterlife is not all harps and clouds. The Council assigns a job to each person, and Riley is to be a Soul Catcher, whose job it is to retrieve the lost souls on Earth who haven't crossed over. She has a guide, the geeky but cute Bodhi, as Riley sets off on her first task. Her first quest is interesting, and Riley proves herself to be a special being.<br /><br /><br />Unfortunately, for me, there were too many unanswered questions as to who certain people are, what is going on in the Here and Now and what is their whole purpose...not to mention what happened to her parents? <br /><br />I was disappointed that Alyson Noel once again set her readers up with too many loose ends, with hopes of tying them up in the next book. <br /><br />Even though I have some issues with the book, I have to admit that I was entertained and found Riley to be extremely likable. Her task was exciting, her voice is sweet and sincere, and I found myself rooting for her. It's a good light read for the 'tween crowd.<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2218150452135818961" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_951577485" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/951577485" />
    <a title="Grace (LovingDemBooks) Z." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9529085-grace-lovingdembooks-z"><img alt="Grace (LovingDemBooks) Z." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1465754864p2/9529085.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/951577485?book_show_action=true">May 29, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Grace (LovingDemBooks) Z." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Grace (LovingDemBooks) Z." href="/user/show/9529085-grace-lovingdembooks-z">Grace (LovingDemBooks) Z.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9529085-grace-lovingdembooks-z?shelf=can-it-get-anymore-cheesy">can-it-get-anymore-cheesy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9529085-grace-lovingdembooks-z?shelf=couldn-t-get-through-this-book">couldn-t-get-through-this-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9529085-grace-lovingdembooks-z?shelf=i-just-can-t">i-just-can-t</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9529085-grace-lovingdembooks-z?shelf=ehhh">ehhh</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer951577485" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13013449563206936417">Buy this book with FREE worldwide shipping: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.bookdepository.com/Radiance-Alyson-Noel/9780312629175/?a_aid=FandomMonthly'>http://www.bookdepository.com/Radianc...</a><br/><br/>1 of 5 stars. This review will probably be very "rantish" or "ramblyish". It's going to be hard writing this. I'm having trouble gathering all of my thoughts. I'm going to straight up say that I really disliked the main character. Riley was immature, selfish, and overly nostalgic. I don't like to be that negative, but I feel like it needs to be said. I wanted to read this book, because I thought it would be a fas</span>
  <span id="freeText13013449563206936417" style="display:none">Buy this book with FREE worldwide shipping: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.bookdepository.com/Radiance-Alyson-Noel/9780312629175/?a_aid=FandomMonthly">http://www.bookdepository.com/Radianc...</a><br /><br />1 of 5 stars. This review will probably be very "rantish" or "ramblyish". It's going to be hard writing this. I'm having trouble gathering all of my thoughts. I'm going to straight up say that I really disliked the main character. Riley was immature, selfish, and overly nostalgic. I don't like to be that negative, but I feel like it needs to be said. I wanted to read this book, because I thought it would be a fast, quick, and fun read. It took me 3 days to get past the first 5 chapters. I'm considered a fast reader, why should it take me of all people 3 days to read 5 chapters?! The chapters are insanely short. The actual concept of this book is quite intriguing. I've only ever heard of a few books focusing on a bridge between life and death, and I've never read any of them. That is probably why I really wanted to read this. I was very disappointed. I don't think I was able to get more than a quarter through the book. First, I really don't think the author of this book Alyson Noel used any imagery at all. Weren't we all taught in school to always use imagery?! <i>Radiance</i> had some of the most vague imagery ever. Second, there really isn't a lot of explanation on what a "radiant" or a "soul catcher" was. Maybe it was explained later in the book, or maybe earlier, but I probably was to bored to read the explanation so I skimmed pages, or the explanation was never there. I'll never know. I think all I can say is that I didn't like it, and that I wouldn't recommend it.<br /><br />My rating system:<br />5 - I don't use the 5 stars. A book is never perfect, therefore a book should never get a 5 star.<br />4 - As good as a book can get. I loved loved loved it.<br />3 - It was good, I enjoyed most of the book, but it has some flaws.<br />2 - I didn't really like it, but at least I got through the book<br />1 - I couldn't get through the book, and I didn't like it.<br /><br />Links:<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://instagram.com/mortalartifices">instagram.com/mortalartifices</a><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://youtube.com/user/LovingDemBooks">youtube.com/user/LovingDemBooks</a><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://instagram.com/grace_zhuang">instagram.com/grace_zhuang</a><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://twitter.com/grayczhuang">twitter.com/grayczhuang</a><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://librarything.com/profile/gracezhuang">librarything.com/profile/gracezhuang</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="13013449563206936417" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1465239613?book_show_action=true">Dec 10, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jo-Jo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jo-Jo" href="/user/show/41053033-jo-jo">Jo-Jo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41053033-jo-jo?shelf=cold-outside">cold-outside</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41053033-jo-jo?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1465239613" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2632272398832658721">There were some things about this book that I found to be refreshingly original. Riley is a typical 12 year old girl in many ways. She loves her family, her dog Buttercup, clothes, music, celebrities, cute boys...and she absolutely looks up to her sister, Ever. Too bad for Riley that her life is cut short when a fatal car accident kills her, her dog, and her mom and dad. Her sister, Ever, is the only one who survives the accident. When Riley finally decides which way to go- with her parents or w</span>
  <span id="freeText2632272398832658721" style="display:none">There were some things about this book that I found to be refreshingly original. Riley is a typical 12 year old girl in many ways. She loves her family, her dog Buttercup, clothes, music, celebrities, cute boys...and she absolutely looks up to her sister, Ever. Too bad for Riley that her life is cut short when a fatal car accident kills her, her dog, and her mom and dad. Her sister, Ever, is the only one who survives the accident. When Riley finally decides which way to go- with her parents or with her sister- she ends up in a place called Here. This is actually the afterlife...where we all go when we die in order to be "placed" in our rightful spot to fulfill our purpose Here since we are no longer on the Earth plain. <br /><br />Like I said, original idea- at least as far as I know I've never read anything like it before. It wasn't bad, it just wasn't outstandingly, blow my mind, fantastic. I kind of feel like it's a book that is aimed more towards younger audiences...it just reads younger - and since the story is written from the POV of a 12 year old girl, I suppose that makes sense. <br /><br />This was a fast read, which is a plus...but not sure I'll continue on with the series...I just don't feel it's really for me. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2632272398832658721" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/167960422?book_show_action=true">May 13, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Leslie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Leslie" href="/user/show/5433591-leslie">Leslie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5433591-leslie?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5433591-leslie?shelf=ghosts">ghosts</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer167960422" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10564955777062552397">I actually read this book because my 11 year old daughter bought it at her school's book fair. To my delight, I realized the author, Alyson Noel, who wrote the YA series, The Immortals, <i>(which I had already read),</i> branched off and wrote this story about The Immortals heroine's deceased sister, "Riley." <br/><br/>I enjoyed Riley's adventures as a ghost who's been assigned a job, as a "Soul Catcher." Her teacher, Bodhi, a cute, seemingly nerdy boy who also seems to be hiding something, explains Riley's new </span>
  <span id="freeText10564955777062552397" style="display:none">I actually read this book because my 11 year old daughter bought it at her school's book fair. To my delight, I realized the author, Alyson Noel, who wrote the YA series, The Immortals, <i>(which I had already read),</i> branched off and wrote this story about The Immortals heroine's deceased sister, "Riley." <br /><br />I enjoyed Riley's adventures as a ghost who's been assigned a job, as a "Soul Catcher." Her teacher, Bodhi, a cute, seemingly nerdy boy who also seems to be hiding something, explains Riley's new job duties...well sort of. Once they return to earth together for Riley’s first assignment, a "Radiant Boy" <i>(someone who needs help crossing over)</i> who's been haunting a castle in England for centuries, is a difficult case. Many Soul Catchers have tried to help him cross over and failed but hopefully, Riley can change his "here and now."<br /><br />This was a very sweet story <i>(and welcomely safe for pre-teens)</i> that left some unanswered questions, but, knowing it will be a series, I wasn't too bothered by that fact. Riley's dog, "Buttercup" was also an endearing character and since I'm a dog lover, made me enjoy the story even more! </span>
  <a data-text-id="10564955777062552397" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer762379668" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11440334058905620292">This book and the next in the series should have a warning label on it, especially since it will show up in elementary school book fairs across the country. It should say warning! This book raises issues about death and the afterlife - parents read first to see if 1) your child is mature enough to handle 2) the crap in it is not a huge conflict with your religious teachings. 3) your kid is able to handle very violent historic images and not get nightmares (shimmer contains images of slave abuse </span>
  <span id="freeText11440334058905620292" style="display:none">This book and the next in the series should have a warning label on it, especially since it will show up in elementary school book fairs across the country. It should say warning! This book raises issues about death and the afterlife - parents read first to see if 1) your child is mature enough to handle 2) the crap in it is not a huge conflict with your religious teachings. 3) your kid is able to handle very violent historic images and not get nightmares (shimmer contains images of slave abuse that are very vivid) I just don't appreciate topics this big and deep handled so carelessly. Writing style, slick, shallow, quick. An easy read. Too easy for the subject matter. Will be disturbing for many kids.</span>

		<td>
		    <b>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('xXmZjRONoRMEuwuk4G8RyAUd6/VsY23u3MfWg2KUiFk57hpvnnQWU7OnX3UTfeBWeKvfFBFUfNAp8n4cvLyWuQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('m1sko0wg03b/O36oMclTaJRbJW2RE+J8Ep/Hp6p/nthnzKdBwdlkNkgnKnnC26L26e0RjOwk80Lnqm84dFeAOA==')})
  }
